    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1368155216" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1368155216" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143126-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406382884p2/3143126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1368155216?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=series-standalone">series-standalone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1368155216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13309027563283779822"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>The second book in the Sea Breeze series brings us the story of Marcus and Willow (Low). I loved Marcus in the first book. As the second-choice love interest he was sweet, caring and a wonderful friend to Sadie, and I was so happy when I discovered that he’d get his HEA in book 2.<br/><br/>Marcus has been away for College but returns to Sea Breeze when his family falls apart – his father has left his mother and is having an affair with a younger woman, leaving his mother completely shattered, and</span>
  <span id="freeText13309027563283779822" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />The second book in the Sea Breeze series brings us the story of Marcus and Willow (Low). I loved Marcus in the first book. As the second-choice love interest he was sweet, caring and a wonderful friend to Sadie, and I was so happy when I discovered that he’d get his HEA in book 2.<br /><br />Marcus has been away for College but returns to Sea Breeze when his family falls apart – his father has left his mother and is having an affair with a younger woman, leaving his mother completely shattered, and his sister all alone to deal with the fallout. He moves into an apartment with serial manwhore Cage York, and that is where he meets Low.<br /><br />Low is Cage’s best friend. She has had a hard life, with a sister who uses her as a babysitter and doesn’t really care for her beyond that. She is technically homeless, although bounces between her sister’s and Cage’s places, but she is such a strong heroine! She’s driven and intelligent, she studies and holds down a part time job, and she is determined to make something of herself. She is also having a hard time with her family, and it is to Cage that she turns. Best friends since childhood, he is her safe place. He is fiercely protective of her, and believes he’s going to marry her one day (once he’s done banging anything with a vagina). Low has no such illusions, but she cares for Cage deeply (as a friend), and she is intrigued by his new roommate. <br /><br />From the beginning of the book, it’s obvious where the story is going to go, but I was happy to just sit back and watch it all unfold. Marcus and Low have an immediate attraction, and even though Cage warns Marcus away from Low, he wants her too much, so he doesn’t let that come between them, instead befriending and pursuing her and being totally swoony about it. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I didn't want to see you, but you invaded my world. Every dark corner you found a way in bringing light to the lifeless and lost."</i>
</blockquote><br />It’s not always easy, they do have some differences they need to overcome, but the relationship develops beautifully, with lots of sweet moments and a little bit of steam, and I really enjoyed watching them together. <br /><br />Although I did have some issues – firstly, I thought the secret keeping was a bit off… <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the fact that they both hide their family dramas from the other was a little bit weird. Here they are opening up to each other, professing love, and obviously creating something special together, but neither of them talk about the thing in their lives that is causing them the most pain and stress. Of course it’s all a part of the build up to the big climax, but still, I thought it was unusual, and the fact that they both kept it a secret is like pointing a big, flashing arrow at it so you know where it’s all going to go. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And that brings me to my big pet peeve for this book – Marcus’ big outburst. Up until that point he had been absolutely wonderful! Sweet, caring, affection and loving, and then all of a sudden he is presented with a situation, completely misreads it and becomes an asshole of massive proportions, behaving in a way that is TOTALLY unreasonable. Seriously, dude, WTF? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ He goes off at Low without even giving her a chance to explain, telling her it’s over and walking away and leaving her alone – which he promised to never do. He then spends the next few months being a total manwhore before he learns of his mistake and suddenly everything changes and he wants her back  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Yes, he apologises, but it’s not enough! And Low forgives him WAY too easily <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I’m glad that she didn’t fall immediately back into his arms, and was prepared to walk away from it all, because he TOTALLY deserved it, but it was still way too fast to be realistic for me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Clearly Low is a better person than I because I’m not sure I would have forgiven him at all! <br /><br />The big surprise in this book for me, was Cage! Yes, he’s a super-slut, but he’s got the biggest heart, and I love the way he loves Low! Their relationship is a little bit twisted (from his side at least), but Low handles it beautifully. They’re such good friends, she leans on him, and he’s there for her, wanting nothing but the best for her. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Okay. If you want to do this thing with Marcus then fine. I’ll take it and deal with it. But when he hurts you. When he lets you down, I’ll be here. My arms are always open for you to run into. I want you happy and if you think this asshole will make you happy then fine. You need to live a little too. I can’t protect you from everything, but I can be here to hold you when he breaks your heart.”</i>
</blockquote><br />The stage is set for Cage’s book up next and I’m looking forward to getting to it. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. The love story is really sweet, and even though there’s a bit of drama (grrrrr), it finishes off in a great place, and I was really happy that Marcus and Low got their happy ending. <br /><br />3.5 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13309027563283779822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BNTLrSKPZRrht2c+WEBXna739cONNmwywtg0HDFbOFoDS1F7waMah4QP09U/f1BBa6OfRgyQt5SKzN3lFo1bRQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('85QvNN9hYC8nLO9xZd6it+IpjqbPVv7/rDf3CebAZqb0C7XiPE0fskKUW5oC4aVrJ33kI07wJVnkIx7wwRYFuQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12365958741829654623">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be Britis</span>
  <span id="freeText12365958741829654623" style="display:none">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be British but alas she was born in Alabama. When asked how many books she has written she has to stop and count on her fingers. When she’s not locked away writing, she is reading, shopping (major shoe and purse addiction), sneaking off to the movies alone, and listening to the drama in her teenagers lives while making mental notes on the good stuff to use later. Don’t judge.<br /><br />You can connect with Abbi online in several different ways. She uses social media to procrastinate.<br /></span>
